The core architecture is built around the abstract CertValidator interface (source/common/tls/cert_validator/cert_validator.h) which defines the contract for certificate validation implementations. The interface includes methods for adding client validation context, verifying certificate chains asynchronously or synchronously, and managing SSL context initialization.\\n\\nThe DefaultCertValidator (source/common/tls/cert_validator/default_validator.h and .cc) provides the primary implementation of X.509 chain verification. It performs certificate validation against a trusted CA store loaded from PEM files and supports certificate pinning through two mechanisms: SHA-256 hash-based pinning (via verifyCertificateHashList) and SPKI (Subject Public Key Information) pinning (via verifyCertificateSpkiList). The validator integrates with the SAN (Subject Alternative Name) matching system for verifying certificate identities.\\n\\nThe SAN matching subsystem is implemented in source/common/tls/cert_validator/san_matcher.h and .cc. The abstract SanMatcher interface defines matching behavior for certificate Subject Alternative Names. The StringSanMatcher implementation provides matching logic for different SAN types: DNS names (GEN_DNS) with special DNS semantics, URI (GEN_URI), email (GEN_EMAIL), IP addresses (GEN_IPADD), and other custom name types (GEN_OTHERNAME) identified by OID. The matcher uses Envoy's string matching framework to support various matching patterns (exact, prefix, suffix, regex, etc.).\\n\\nCertificates and their associated OCSP responses are managed by the ContextImpl class (source/common/tls/context_impl.h and .cc). The ContextImpl maintains a vector of TlsContext structures, each containing an SSL_CTX, the certificate chain (X509), the certificate file path, and an OcspResponseWrapper for OCSP stapling. The class also holds a CertValidatorPtr that performs the actual certificate validation. The ContextImpl implements callbacks for custom certificate verification (customVerifyCallback, customVerifyCertChain) that integrate with OpenSSL's verification pipeline.\\n\\nThe ServerContextImpl (source/common/tls/server_context_impl.h and .cc) extends ContextImpl to handle server-side TLS operations including OCSP stapling. The server context selects appropriate certificate contexts based on ClientHello details and determines OCSP stapling capability (OcspStapleAction enum). The findTlsContext method handles certificate selection with optional OCSP response stapling for compatible clients.\\n\\nOCSP response support is implemented in the source/common/tls/ocsp/ directory. The ocsp.h file defines ASN.1 structures for OCSP responses including OcspResponse (top-level structure), BasicOcspResponse (RFC 6960 compliant response type), ResponseData (containing certificate statuses), and SingleResponse (status for a single certificate). The OcspResponseWrapperImpl class wraps DER-encoded OCSP responses and provides methods to check response validity and expiration (secondsUntilExpiration, isExpired, getThisUpdate, getNextUpdate). The wrapper can match responses to specific certificates via matchesCertificate.\\n\\nASN.1 DER parsing for OCSP structures is handled by the Asn1OcspUtility class in source/common/tls/ocsp/asn1_utility.h and .cc. This utility provides parser functions for all OCSP structures: parseOcspResponse (top-level), parseResponseStatus, parseResponseBytes, parseBasicOcspResponse, parseResponseData, parseSingleResponse, and parseCertId. These functions use OpenSSL's CBS (Crypto Byte String) API for safe parsing of DER-encoded data.\\n\\nThe certificate validator factory pattern is implemented in source/common/tls/cert_validator/factory.h and .cc. The CertValidatorFactory abstract class creates CertValidator instances based on configuration. Additional validator implementations include the SPIFFEValidator (source/extensions/transport_sockets/tls/cert_validator/spiffe/spiffe_validator.h and .cc) which implements SPIFFE (Secure Production Identity Framework For Everyone) certificate validation with trust domain and URI SAN matching.\\n\\nCertificate validation configuration is managed by certificate_validation_context_config_impl.h and .cc which provides the configuration interface for specifying trusted CA certificates, verification policies, and validation rules. The complete pipeline integrates X.509 chain verification, SAN matching, certificate pinning, OCSP response validation, and asynchronous callback mechanisms to provide flexible and secure certificate validation for both client and server TLS contexts.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":11,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1971,"cache_read_input_tokens":53833,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":1971},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"d13392da-510d-43ae-b93d-c3e751e85485","uuid":"c88302ca-cdba-461f-941a-4336aea85bc0"}

The core architecture is built around the abstract CertValidator interface (source/common/tls/cert_validator/cert_validator.h) which defines the contract for certificate validation implementations. The interface includes methods for adding client validation context, verifying certificate chains asynchronously or synchronously, and managing SSL context initialization.\\n\\nThe DefaultCertValidator (source/common/tls/cert_validator/default_validator.h and .cc) provides the primary implementation of X.509 chain verification. It performs certificate validation against a trusted CA store loaded from PEM files and supports certificate pinning through two mechanisms: SHA-256 hash-based pinning (via verifyCertificateHashList) and SPKI (Subject Public Key Information) pinning (via verifyCertificateSpkiList). The validator integrates with the SAN (Subject Alternative Name) matching system for verifying certificate identities.\\n\\nThe SAN matching subsystem is implemented in source/common/tls/cert_validator/san_matcher.h and .cc. The abstract SanMatcher interface defines matching behavior for certificate Subject Alternative Names. The StringSanMatcher implementation provides matching logic for different SAN types: DNS names (GEN_DNS) with special DNS semantics, URI (GEN_URI), email (GEN_EMAIL), IP addresses (GEN_IPADD), and other custom name types (GEN_OTHERNAME) identified by OID. The matcher uses Envoy's string matching framework to support various matching patterns (exact, prefix, suffix, regex, etc.).\\n\\nCertificates and their associated OCSP responses are managed by the ContextImpl class (source/common/tls/context_impl.h and .cc). The ContextImpl maintains a vector of TlsContext structures, each containing an SSL_CTX, the certificate chain (X509), the certificate file path, and an OcspResponseWrapper for OCSP stapling. The class also holds a CertValidatorPtr that performs the actual certificate validation. The ContextImpl implements callbacks for custom certificate verification (customVerifyCallback, customVerifyCertChain) that integrate with OpenSSL's verification pipeline.\\n\\nThe ServerContextImpl (source/common/tls/server_context_impl.h and .cc) extends ContextImpl to handle server-side TLS operations including OCSP stapling. The server context selects appropriate certificate contexts based on ClientHello details and determines OCSP stapling capability (OcspStapleAction enum). The findTlsContext method handles certificate selection with optional OCSP response stapling for compatible clients.\\n\\nOCSP response support is implemented in the source/common/tls/ocsp/ directory. The ocsp.h file defines ASN.1 structures for OCSP responses including OcspResponse (top-level structure), BasicOcspResponse (RFC 6960 compliant response type), ResponseData (containing certificate statuses), and SingleResponse (status for a single certificate). The OcspResponseWrapperImpl class wraps DER-encoded OCSP responses and provides methods to check response validity and expiration (secondsUntilExpiration, isExpired, getThisUpdate, getNextUpdate). The wrapper can match responses to specific certificates via matchesCertificate.\\n\\nASN.1 DER parsing for OCSP structures is handled by the Asn1OcspUtility class in source/common/tls/ocsp/asn1_utility.h and .cc. This utility provides parser functions for all OCSP structures: parseOcspResponse (top-level), parseResponseStatus, parseResponseBytes, parseBasicOcspResponse, parseResponseData, parseSingleResponse, and parseCertId. These functions use OpenSSL's CBS (Crypto Byte String) API for safe parsing of DER-encoded data.\\n\\nThe certificate validator factory pattern is implemented in source/common/tls/cert_validator/factory.h and .cc. The CertValidatorFactory abstract class creates CertValidator instances based on configuration. Additional validator implementations include the SPIFFEValidator (source/extensions/transport_sockets/tls/cert_validator/spiffe/spiffe_validator.h and .cc) which implements SPIFFE (Secure Production Identity Framework For Everyone) certificate validation with trust domain and URI SAN matching.\\n\\nCertificate validation configuration is managed by certificate_validation_context_config_impl.h and .cc which provides the configuration interface for specifying trusted CA certificates, verification policies, and validation rules.
